Resolving the Muqarana Objection in the Hal
Resolving the muqarana objection via extended operator

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify a muqarana objection in a classical usul text and apply the Hanafi commentator's method of rescuing temporal coincidence by reinterpreting the operator as an extended customary act.

Core Idea
A grammatical violation is avoided by shifting the operator from a specific moment to a customary extended beginning.

This passage from the sharh (commentary) demonstrates a common technique in Hanafi usul textual analysis: resolving an apparent violation of a grammatical rule (here, the temporal coincidence of the hal with its operator) by reinterpreting the scope of the operator. The objection is that the hal 'hamidan' (praising) seems to occur after the basmalah, violating muqarana. The commentator shows that the true operator is not the specific utterance of the basmalah but the extended customary beginning of the book, thus preserving grammatical coherence.

Guided Path
1
Identify the grammatical rule
Recall the rule: the circumstantial accusative (hal) must coincide in time with its operator (amil). The objector argues that 'hamidan' praises after the basmalah, so the times do not match.
This rule is a standard principle of Arabic grammar (nahw) applied to the analysis of the author's phrasing.
2
Recognize the objection
The objector assumes the operator is 'abtadi' (I begin) with the basmalah, which ends quickly. Since praise follows, the hal cannot be simultaneous.
The objection challenges the grammatical validity of the author's choice of words.
3
Analyze the commentator's resolution
The commentator denies that the ba' of basmalah is attached to 'abtadi'. Instead, the ba' belongs to a hidden verb 'mutabarrik' (seeking blessing), and the entire phrase 'mutabarrikan' is itself a hal. The operator for all these ahwal is the absolute customary beginning (al-ibtida' al-urfī al-mumtadd), which extends from the start of authorship into the research phase.
The shift from a punctual to an extended operator restores muqarana.
4
Understand the second objection
A further objection: if we interpret 'hamid' as 'intending praise' (a future intention) to match the extended operator, then we combine literal and figurative meanings. The commentator resolves this by positing a deletion: 'hamid thaniyan' (praising intending), so it is purely figurative without combining.
The commentator uses the principle of deletion (hadhf) to avoid the problem.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قال الشارح : فإن قلت : من شرط الحال المقارنة للعامل والأحوال المذكورة أعنى حامدا وغيره لاتقارن الابتداء بالتسمية . قلت : ليس الباء صلة لابتداء بل الظرف حال والمعنى تبركا باسم الله أبتدئ الكتاب والابتداء أمر عرفي ممتد من حين الأخذ في التصنيف إلى الشروع في البحث . ويقارنه التبرك بالتسمية والحمد والصلاة . لغوی تحقیق: المقارنة : از باب مفاعلہ، ملایا ہوا "صلة": چمٹا ہوا ہونا یہاں پر اس سے مراد متعلق ہے ممند: از امتداد کھینچا ہوا" الأخذ " لینا، یہاں اس سے مراد شروع ہوتا ہے۔ تشریح مصنف کی اس عبارت کی غرض ایک سوال کا جواب دینا ہے سوال فان قلت ... الخ علم نحو کا قانون ہے کہ حال اور اس کے عامل میں مقارنت ضروری ہوتی ہے، یعنی حال اور اس کے عامل دونوں کا زمانہ ایک ہوتا ہے، مثلا : جاء نی زید را کبا میں جو آنے کا زمانہ ہے وہی بعینہ سوار ہونے کا زمانہ ہے۔ تو اب سوال ہے کہ یہاں حمد اور ابتدا بالقسمیہ کا زمانہ ایک نہیں تو اس لیے کہ عامل یعنی ابتدا بالتسمیہ ختم ہو جاتی ہے اس کے بعد حامدا سے حمد شروع ہوتی ہے تو زمانہ ایک نہ ہوا۔ جواب قلت .... إلخ جواب کا حاصل یہ ہے کہ بسم اللہ کی باء کا متعلق ابتدئ نہیں بلکہ "متبر کا ہے اور متبرکا بھی حامدا " ، "مصلیا کی طرح حال ہے اور سب کا عامل مطلق ابتدا ہے۔ مطلق ابتدا ایک امر عرفی محمد ہے، جس کی حمدہ تسمیہ اور صلاح سب کے ساتھ مقارنت ثابت ہو جائے گی ، کیونکہ آپ کتاب کے چند اوراق پڑھ جائیں پھر بھی ابتدا شمار ہوگی اگر بسم اللہ کی باء کا تعلق ابتدئ سے ہوتا تو پھر واقعی ابتدا تسمیہ کے ساتھ مقید ہو جاتی جو بسم الله الرحمن الرحیم کی میم تک ختم ہو جاتی اور حمد کا علیحدہ زمانہ بعد میں ہوتا جس سے مقارنت والی شرط مفقود ہو جاتی لیکن پہلے ہم وضاحت کر چکے ہیں کہ بسم الله کا متعلق متبر کا ہے فاندفع الاشكال ۔ قال الشارح : فإن قلت: فعلى الوجه الثالث يكون حامدا ثانيا بمعنى عازما عليه وناويا الحمد ، ليكون مقارنا للعامل وح يلزم الجمع بين الحقيقة والمجاز . قلت : يجعل من قبيل المحذوف أى : حامد اثانيا بمعنى عازما عليه فلا يلزم الجمع بين الحقيقة والمجاز .
The commentator said: If you say: It is a condition of the circumstantial accusative (hal) that it coincides in time with its operator, and the mentioned states (halat) – i.e., praising (hamid) and others – do not coincide with the beginning (ibtida') with the basmalah. I say: The ba' of basmalah is not attached to 'ibtida' but rather the adverb (zarf) is the hal, and the meaning is: 'Seeking blessing by the name of Allah I begin the book, and the beginning is a customary matter, extending from the time of starting authorship until the start of research. And the seeking of blessing by the basmalah, praise, and salutation coincides with it.' Linguistic research: al-muqaranah: from bab mufa'alah, made to coincide. 'silah': attached, here it means related. 'mumtadd': from imtidad, stretched. 'al-akhdh': taking, here it means beginning. Explanation: The purpose of this phrase of the author is to answer a question. The question: The science of grammar rules that there must be coincidence between the hal and its operator, i.e., their time is the same. For example, 'jaani Zaydun rakiban' (Zayd came riding) – the time of coming is exactly the time of riding. So the question is: Here the time of praise and the time of beginning with the basmalah are not the same, because the operator, i.e., the beginning with the basmalah, ends, and after it, praise begins with 'hamid', so the times are not the same. Answer: The essence of the answer is that the ba' of basmalah is not attached to 'abtadi'' but to 'mutabarrik' and 'mutabarrikan' is like 'hamidan', 'musalliyan' a hal, and the operator for all is the absolute beginning (al-ibtida' al-mutlaq). The absolute beginning is a customary matter, extended, which will be shown to coincide with the praise, basmalah, and salutation because if you read several folios of the book, it will still be considered the beginning. If the ba' of basmalah were attached to 'abtadi'', then the beginning would be restricted to the basmalah, which ends with the meem of 'al-rahim', and praise would be at a separate subsequent time, rendering the condition of coincidence void. But we have already clarified that the basmalah's ba' is attached to 'mutabarrik', so the objection is repelled. The commentator said: If you say: According to the third interpretation, 'hamid' (praising) is with the meaning of 'determined to do it and intending praise', so that it coincides with the operator, and that would necessitate combining the literal and figurative meanings. I say: It is considered as a case of deletion, i.e., 'hamid thaniyan' meaning 'determined to do it', so there is no need to combine literal and figurative meanings.
Source pages p. 22

Commentary
This passage is a grammatical discussion from the sharh. It addresses a grammatical objection: the hal (circumstantial accusative) must coincide in time with its operator. In the author's phrasing, the hal 'hamidan' (praising) seems to occur after the basmalah, so it does not coincide. The commentator resolves this by arguing that the operator is not the specific 'beginning with basmalah' but the absolute customary beginning of the book, which extends over time. Thus the hal can coincide. Additionally, a second objection about combining literal and figurative meaning is resolved by interpreting 'hamid' as intending praise (figurative) rather than actual praise.

Key Terms
حال (hal): circumstantial accusative indicating state
مقارنة (muqarana): temporal coincidence between hal and operator
صلة (sila): attachment/relation, here the grammatical relation of the particle to the verb
ابتداء (ibtida'): beginning, here the act of starting the book
حذف (hadhf): deletion, a grammatical device to avoid combining literal and figurative

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the commentator, what is the true operator (amil) of the hal 'hamidan'?
A) The word 'abtadi' (I begin)
B) The basmalah phrase 'bismillah'
C) The absolute customary beginning of the book (al-ibtida' al-urfī)
D) The verb 'mutabarrik' (seeking blessing)

Key Takeaway
When a grammatical condition appears violated in a classical text, re-examining the scope of the operator—such as shifting from a punctual to an extended customary act—can resolve the apparent inconsistency.

Resolving the Simultaneity Objection: Hal and Factor in the Basmalah
Resolving a grammatical objection via customary extension

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi usul principle of 'urf (custom) to resolve grammatical objections in textual interpretation, specifically regarding the simultaneity condition of hal and its factor.

Core Idea
The absolute beginning is a customary extended matter—it does not end with the basmalah, thus the hal is simultaneous.

In this passage, the author addresses a grammatical objection to the opening phrase of many Hanafi works: how can the basmalah and the hamd share the same time if the basmalah ends before the hamd begins? The answer relies on a key Hanafi usul insight: the 'beginning' of a book is not a punctual event but a customary extended process. This lesson walks you through the objection, the response, and the underlying methodology.

Guided Path
1
Identify the objection
What grammatical rule is violated in the opening phrase? The rule of muqaranah requires simultaneity between the hal and its factor.
The objection points out that the basmalah ends before the hamd begins, breaking simultaneity.
2
Locate the response
How does the author resolve it? By stating that the ba' of bismillah is attached to an implied 'mutabarrikan', not to 'abtadi'.
This shifts the factor from a punctual verb to the absolute beginning.
3
Understand the key concept
What is al-ibtida' al-mutlaq? It is the absolute beginning, defined as a customary extended matter from the start of writing to the end of research.
It is not a moment but a span.
4
Recognize the role of 'urf
Custom ('urf) extends the temporal scope of the beginning so that the basmalah, hamd, and salawat all occur within it.
This satisfies the simultaneity condition in a customary sense.
5
Apply to similar contexts
How would you use this principle in other texts? Whenever a grammatical rule seems violated by a common phrase, consider whether custom extends the meaning.
This is a standard Hanafi approach in usul.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
والمعنى تبـركـا بـاسـم الله أبتدئ الكتاب والابتداء أمر عرفي ممتد من حين الأخذ في التصنيف إلى الشروع في البحث . ويقارنه التبرك بالتسمية والحمد والصلاة . لغوی تحقیق: الـمـقــارنـة »: از باب مفاعلہ، ملایا ہوا ”صلة “: چمٹا ہوا ہونا یہاں پر اس سے مراد متعلق ہے ممند: از امتداد کھینچا ہوا" الأخذ " لینا، یہاں اس سے مراد شروع ہوتا ہے۔ تشریح مصنف کی اس عبارت کی غرض ایک سوال کا جواب دینا ہے سوال فان قلت ... الخ علم نحو کا قانون ہے کہ حال اور اس کے عامل میں مقارنت ضروری ہوتی ہے، یعنی حال اور اس کے عامل دونوں کا زمانہ ایک ہوتا ہے، مثلا : جاء نی زید را کبا میں جو آنے کا زمانہ ہے وہی بعینہ سوار ہونے کا زمانہ ہے۔ تو اب سوال ہے کہ یہاں حمد اور ابتدا بالقسمیہ کا زمانہ ایک نہیں تو اس لیے کہ عامل یعنی ابتدا بالتسمیہ ختم ہو جاتی ہے اس کے بعد حامدا سے حمد شروع ہوتی ہے تو زمانہ ایک نہ ہوا۔ قلت .... إلخ جواب کا حاصل یہ ہے کہ بسم اللہ کی باء کا متعلق ابتدئ نہیں بلکہ ”متبر کا ہے اور متبرکا بھی حامدا “ ، ”مصلیا کی طرح حال ہے اور سب کا عامل مطلق ابتدا ہے۔ مطلق ابتدا ایک امر عرفی ممتد ہے، جس کی حمدہ تسمیہ اور صلاح سب کے ساتھ مقارنت ثابت ہو جائے گی ، کیونکہ آپ کتاب کے چند اوراق پڑھ جائیں پھر بھی ابتدا شمار ہوگی اگر بسم اللہ کی باء کا تعلق ابتدئ سے ہوتا تو پھر واقعی ابتدا تسمیہ کے ساتھ مقید ہو جاتی جو بسم الله الرحمن الرحیم کی میم تک ختم ہو جاتی اور حمد کا علیحدہ زمانہ بعد میں ہوتا جس سے مقارنت والی شرط مفقود ہو جاتی لیکن پہلے ہم وضاحت کر چکے ہیں کہ بسم الله کا متعلق متبر کا ہے فاندفع الاشكال ۔
And the meaning: seeking blessing with the name of Allah I begin the book, and the beginning is a customary extended matter from the time of starting the writing to the commencement of research. And the seeking of blessing by the basmalah, the hamd, and the salawat accompanies it. Linguistic investigation: 'al-muqāranah': from the bāb of mufā'alah, to accompany. 'ṣilah': to be attached. Here, what is meant by it is connection. 'mumtadd': from imtidād, stretched. 'al-akhdh': taking, here what is meant by it is beginning. Explanation: The purpose of this expression of the author is to answer a question: A question: The rule of the science of grammar is that simultaneity is necessary between the ḥāl and its factor, i.e., the time of the ḥāl and the time of its factor are one. For example, in 'jā'anī Zaydun rākiban', the time of coming is exactly the time of riding. So now the question is that here the time of the hamd and the time of the beginning with the basmalah are not one, because the factor, i.e., the beginning with the basmalah, ends after this and the hamd begins from 'ḥāmidan', so the time was not one. The response: The summary of the answer is that the bā of bismillāh is not related to 'abtadi' but rather to 'mutabarrikan', and 'mutabarrikan' like 'ḥāmidan' and 'muṣalliyan' is a ḥāl, and the factor of all is the absolute beginning. The absolute beginning is an extended customary matter, so its simultaneity with the hamd, the basmalah, and the salāh is established, because if you read several leaves of the book, it will still be considered the beginning. If the bā of bismillāh were related to 'abtadi', then indeed the beginning would be restricted to the basmalah, which ends at the mīm of bismillāh al-raḥmān al-rahīm, and the time of the hamd would be separate afterwards, causing the condition of simultaneity to be missing. But we have already clarified that the bā of bismillāh is related to 'mutabarrikan', so the objection is repelled.
Source pages p. 23

Commentary
This passage is a commentary on the opening lines of the matn, addressing a grammatical objection regarding the state (ḥāl) construction. The objection is that the factor (ʿāmil) 'abtadi' and the ḥāl 'ḥāmidan' do not share the same time, violating the rule of simultaneity. The response clarifies that the bā in bismillāh does not attach to 'abtadi' but to an implied 'mutabarrikan' (seeking blessing), which itself is a ḥāl. The factor of all these ḥāls is the 'absolute beginning' (al-ibtidāʾ al-muṭlaq), which is a customary, extended matter – it does not end with the utterance of the basmalah but continues as long as the author is in the process of writing the book. Hence, the ḥāl and its factor are simultaneous in a customary sense. This reasoning is based on the Hanafi usul principle that customary practices (ʿurf) can extend the temporal scope of linguistic acts.

Key Terms
حال (ḥāl): A noun in the accusative describing the condition of the subject at the time of the action; requires simultaneity with its factor.
ابتداء (ibtidāʾ): The beginning; here the absolute beginning (al-ibtidāʾ al-muṭlaq) which is a customary extended matter.
مقارنة (muqāranah): The condition of simultaneity between the ḥāl and its factor.
متبركا (mutabarrikan): Seeking blessing; an implied word to which the bā of bismillāh is attached, serving as a ḥāl.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the response, what is the factor (ʿāmil) of 'ḥāmidan' and 'muṣalliyan'?
A) 'abtadi' (I begin)
B) The absolute beginning (al-ibtidāʾ al-muṭlaq)
C) The basmalah
D) The word 'mutabarrikan'

Key Takeaway
The absolute beginning (al-ibtidāʾ al-muṭlaq) is a customary extended matter, allowing the ḥāls of basmalah, hamd, and salāh to share simultaneity with their factor.

Explaining the Sequence of Salawat after Hamd
Explaining the reason for salawat after hamd

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi usul principle that links the sending of salawat after hamd to the Prophet's role as intermediary for the greatest blessing (Islam).

Core Idea
Salawat follows hamd because the Prophet is the conduit of Islam, the greatest blessing.

This passage from the commentary on Al-Tawzeeh wa al-Talweeh explains why the author of the matn placed salawat (blessings on the Prophet) immediately after hamd (praise of Allah). The commentator provides a teleological reason: since the greatest blessing to reach humanity is Islam, and it came through the Prophet, it is natural to honor him after honoring Allah. This reflects the Hanafi approach to textual coherence and reverence.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two elements
Recognize that the text begins with hamd (praise of Allah) and immediately follows with salawat (blessings on the Prophet).
The hamd is for Allah, salawat is for the Prophet.
2
Understand the commentator's reasoning
The greatest blessing (Islam) reaches the servant through the Prophet's mediation, so it is fitting to invoke blessings on him after praising the Giver of the blessing.
The sequence is not arbitrary; it reflects a causal relationship.
3
Analyze the logical sequence
Praise the source of the blessing (Allah) and then the intermediary (the Prophet) as a form of gratitude and honoring.
This is a common pattern in Hanafi texts.
4
Note the omission of the Prophet's name
The omission is deliberate (tanwih) to exalt and to indicate that his status as best of messengers is obvious.
This is a literary device for veneration.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قال الشارح : وعلى أفضل رسله مصليا ، لما كان أجل النعم الواصلة إلى العبد هو دين الإسلام ، وبه التوصل إلى النعيم الدائم في دار السلام ، وذلك بتوسط النبي - عليه السلام صار الدعاء له تلو الثناء على الله تعالى ، فأردف الحمد بالصلاة وفي ترك التصريح باسم النبي - صلى الله عليه وسلم - على ما في النسخة المقرؤة .. تنويه نشانه و تنبيه على أن كونه أفضل الرسل أمر جلى لا يخفى على أحد. لغوی تحقیق: اجل : بزرگ بڑا نعم نعمت کی جمع التوصل “ : پہنچنا دار السلام »: بهشت "لو" (بالکسر) پیچھے اُردف : از ارداف ایک شی کو دوسری مٹی کے پیچھے لانا " تسویه ": باب تفعیل کا مصدر ہے ، قصد کرنا۔ تشریح Maktaba Tul Ishaat.com
The commentator said: And upon the best of His messengers praying, because the greatest of blessings reaching the servant is the religion of Islam, and by it is the means to eternal bliss in the abode of peace, and that is through the mediation of the Prophet - peace be upon him. So supplication for him follows praise of Allah Almighty, so he appended the hamd with salawat. And in omitting explicit mention of the name of the Prophet - peace be upon him - according to the recited copy is an exaltation and an indication that his being the best of messengers is an obvious matter not hidden from anyone. Linguistic investigation: 'ajall': great, big. 'niʿam': plural of blessing. 'altawṣul': reaching. 'dār al-salām': paradise. 'luw' (with kasra): behind. 'urdif': from irdāf, to bring one thing after another. 'taswiyah': is the masdar of bāb tafʿīl, to intend. Explanation: [incomplete]
Source pages p. 24

Commentary
This passage explains why the author mentions salawat (prayers upon the Prophet) after the hamd (praise of Allah). The reason is that the greatest blessing that reaches a servant is the religion of Islam, and through Islam one attains eternal bliss in Paradise, and that comes through the mediation of the Prophet. Therefore, invoking blessings upon the Prophet follows naturally after praising Allah. The commentator also notes that the omission of the explicit name of the Prophet in some copies is a deliberate exaltation (tanwīh) and a reminder that his status as the best of messengers is so obvious it needs no mention. This reflects the Hanafi reverence for the Prophet and the literary style of the text.

Key Terms
الصلاة (al-ṣalāh): Supplication and blessings upon the Prophet; here it is appended to hamd as a form of following praise.
أفضل الرسل (afḍal al-rusul): The best of messengers; referring to Prophet Muhammad, indicating his highest status among all prophets.
تنويه (tanwīh): Exaltation or raising the status; here it refers to the omission of the Prophet's name to honor him.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the commentator, why is salawat mentioned immediately after hamd?
A) Because it is a linguistic requirement
B) Because the greatest blessing (Islam) reaches through the Prophet, so prayer for him follows praise of Allah
C) Because the Prophet commanded it
D) To make the text longer

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi usul texts, the sequence of hamd followed by salawat is not arbitrary but is based on the theological recognition that the Prophet is the intermediary for the greatest blessing (Islam).

6 min
Why the Author Did Not Explicitly Name the Prophet
Explains why the matn author omitted explicit naming of the Prophet.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify and explain the reasons for textual omission of the Prophet's name in the matn, and apply the Hanafi principle of adab in interpreting such omissions.

Core Idea
Omitting the Prophet's name is a sign of profound respect—not a flaw—showing the description alone suffices.

In this short passage from al-Talwih, the commentator addresses why the matn author omitted explicit mention of the Prophet ﷺ's name. Understanding this seemingly minor textual choice reveals a key Hanafi methodological principle: that respect (adab) can override formal precision, and that textual variants must be handled with care. Let us explore the reasoning.

Guided Path
1
Identify the textual anomaly
Recognize that the matn uses 'علي أفضل رسله' instead of 'علي محمد أفضل رسله'. The name is omitted.
2
Recognize the presumed question
The commentator anticipates a reader's question: why not name explicitly? This shows a common expectation of precision.
3
Examine the commentator's response
Two reasons: (1) there are two copies, one with name, one without; (2) omitting shows respect (like not calling father by name) and the description alone is sufficient.
4
Extract the Hanafi principle
Note that the principle of adab (respect) influences even textual expression in legal works. Omission is deliberate and meaningful.

'And regarding the meaning of omitting explicit mention... etc.' He is answering a presumed question: Why did the matn author not explicitly mention the name of the Prophet ﷺ? Instead of saying 'Ali Afdal Ruslihi', why not say 'Ali Muhammad'? Answer: There are two copies of the text. In one, the name is explicit; no question arises. In the other copy, which the author read, there is no explicit mention. The point is out of regard for his high status, explicit mention was omitted, because naming someone can be a kind of disrespect, just as calling one's father by name is considered disrespectful, while saying 'father' shows honor. Additionally, omitting explicit mention alerts that the one described as 'best of messengers' is only him, so explicit mention is unnecessary.
Source pages p. 25

Commentary
This passage addresses a textual anomaly in the matn (the base text). The commentator explains why the author did not write the Prophet's name explicitly. He provides two reasons: respect (similar to avoiding parent's name) and rhetorical elegance (the description alone suffices). This reflects Hanafi attention to textual nuance and balaghah.

Key Terms

The Methodological Foundation: Logic in Hanafi Usul
Explaining the methodological foundation of the book in logic.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the role of logic (mantiq) as the structural foundation of later Hanafi usul works, and differentiate this from earlier informal methods.

Core Idea
Later Hanafi usul is systematically built on logical rules, not on mere practical attainment.

This passage from a commentary on Al-Tawdih wa al-Talwih clarifies that the book is 'founded on the rules of the rational intellect.' The commentator identifies these rules as the science of logic (ilm al-mizan). This marks a shift from earlier Hanafi methodology, where scholars were content with reaching the desired legal outcome without explicit logical scaffolding. Understanding this sets the stage for appreciating the rigour of later usul works.

Guided Path
1
Identify the key phrase
Locate the phrase 'qawa'id al-ma'qul' (rules of the rational) in the passage. This is the central claim about the book's foundation.
The phrase is explicatory of the matn's description.
2
Understand the commentator's equation
The commentator equates 'qawa'id al-ma'qul' with 'ilm al-mizan' (science of measurement). Recognize that this is a direct reference to logic (mantiq).
In Hanafi usul, 'ilm al-mizan' is a common synonym for Aristotelian logic.
3
Contrast with earlier practice
Note the contrast: 'not as was the custom of the early shaykhs of being content with attaining the objective.' Earlier scholars did not feel the need to systematically apply logical rules.
This highlights a methodological evolution within the Hanafi school.
4
Recognize the commentator's purpose
The commentator is explaining that the matn author is highlighting a distinctive feature of his work: its rigorous logical structure.
This sets the expectation that the work will follow precise definitions and reasoning steps.

Hierarchy of Islamic Sciences: Kalam, Usul, Fiqh
Defining key terms and establishing the hierarchy of Islamic sciences.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to define Shari'a, Usul al-Shari'a, and Furu' al-Shari'a and explain the hierarchical dependency among Kalam, Usul al-Fiqh, and Fiqh.

Core Idea
Fiqh depends on Usul, Usul depends on Kalam – knowledge of Allah is the foundation of all legal rulings.

Before diving into the detailed rulings of fiqh or the principles of usul, we must understand where these disciplines stand in the broader landscape of Islamic knowledge. This passage from the commentary on Al-Tawdih lays out the key definitions and the essential hierarchy: the science of Kalam (theology) provides the foundation, Usul al-Fiqh builds upon it, and Fiqh derives from Usul. Grasping this ordering is crucial for anyone who wishes to engage in rigorous istinbat (derivation of rulings) because it clarifies the dependencies and the scope of each discipline.

Guided Path
1
Identify the core definitions
Extract the precise definitions of Shari'a, Usul al-Shari'a (universal proofs), and Furu' al-Shari'a (detailed rulings) as given in the passage. Note that Shari'a includes both fiqh and creedal matters proven by transmitted proofs.
Hanafi view: Shari'a is not limited to fiqh; it encompasses beliefs as well.
2
Understand 'Mabani al-Usul' and 'Tamhid al-Mabani'
The passage explains that the 'foundations of the principles' (Mabani al-Usul) is the science of Tawhid (Kalam) upon which the universal proofs depend. 'Tamhid al-Mabani' means to straighten and correct these foundations according to truth.
Without establishing the existence and attributes of Allah, the Qur'an and Sunnah cannot be used as proofs.
3
Trace the hierarchical dependency
The passage explicitly states that knowledge of partial rulings (Fiqh) depends on knowledge of universal proofs (Usul al-Fiqh), and that in turn depends on knowledge of the Creator, His attributes, and prophethood (Kalam).
Thus Kalam is the highest, then Usul al-Fiqh, then Fiqh.
4
Recognize the blessing of 'diraka' and 'al-ma'ani'
The passage notes that the subtlety of the detailed causes ('al-ma'ani') of each ruling is a blessing that elevates scholars. This subtlety is the domain of mujtahids.
This reinforces the importance of deep study of usul and the need for qualified jurists.

السابقة . شبه
And similar to that. The principles of Sharia are its universal proofs, and the foundations of the principles are what they are based upon from the knowledge of the Essence, Attributes, and Prophecies. Their preparation is their straightening and correction by being in accordance with the truth and the path of correctness. The branches of Sharia are its detailed rulings built in the science of Fiqh. And their meanings are the detailed partial causes for every issue, and their subtlety is that they are delicate and obscure, not easily accessible to everyone. And all that are blessings deserving praise, for through Sharia the order of the world and the reward of the Hereafter. And through the subtlety of the meanings of Fiqh, the ranks of scholars are elevated and they attain reward in the abode of recompense. In this speech there is an indication that the science of Principles is above Fiqh and below Theology (Kalam), because knowledge of partial rulings with their detailed proofs is dependent on knowledge of the states of universal proofs in that they lead to legal rulings, and that is dependent on knowledge of the Exalted Creator, His attributes, the truthfulness of the messenger, the indication of his miracles, and the like, which are included in the science of Kalam, which investigates the states of the Creator, prophethood, Imamate, the return, and related matters according to Islamic law. (Then linguistic research and commentary in Urdu follow.)
Source pages p. 42

Commentary
This passage is a commentary from the sharh of Al-Tawdih, expanding on the definitions of key terms. The author begins by defining 'Sharia' as encompassing both fiqh and other matters proven by transmitted proofs (like the vision of Allah in the hereafter, resurrection, the authority of consensus and analogy). 'Usul al-Sharia' refers to the universal proofs: Qur'an, Sunnah, Ijma', and Qiyas. 'Mabani al-Usul' (foundations of the principles) is the science on which these proofs depend for their establishment, namely Tawhid (theology), because without proving the existence of Allah, the Qur'an cannot be established. 'Tamhid al-Mabani' means to straighten these foundations according to truth. 'Furu' al-Sharia' are the detailed rulings of fiqh. 'Ma'ani' (meanings) refer to the partial causes for each fiqh ruling, e.g., the prohibition of cannabis is due to its intoxicating effect, a detailed cause. The subtlety of these causes is that only mujtahid scholars can access them. The author then defends that these are genuine blessings: through Sharia, worldly order and otherworldly reward are achieved; through the subtlety of proofs, scholars attain high ranks. An important point is the hierarchy of the three Islamic sciences: Kalam (theology) is highest, then Usul al-Fiqh, then Fiqh. This is because fiqh rulings depend on usul al-fiqh (knowledge of proofs), and usul al-fiqh depends on kalam (knowledge of the Creator). The passage concludes with a note that the definition of 'ilm al-kalam here excludes philosophy, being based on Islamic law rather than reason alone.

Key Terms
شريعة (Shari'a): The divine law consisting of all rulings proven by transmitted proofs, including fiqh and other creedal matters.
أصول الشريعة (Usul al-Shari'a): The universal proofs of Shari'a: Qur'an, Sunnah, Ijma', Qiyas.
فروع الشريعة (Furu' al-Shari'a): The detailed rulings derived from the principles, i.e., fiqh.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the correct hierarchy of the three Islamic sciences?
A) Fiqh, Usul al-Fiqh, Kalam
B) Kalam, Fiqh, Usul al-Fiqh
C) Kalam, Usul al-Fiqh, Fiqh
D) Usul al-Fiqh, Kalam, Fiqh

Key Takeaway
Fiqh depends on Usul, Usul depends on Kalam – the hierarchy ensures that all legal derivation rests on a sound theological foundation.

The Two Definitions of Usul al-Fiqh: Idafi and Laqabi
Explaining the two types of definition for Usul al-Fiqh and their order

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between the idafi and laqabi definitions of Usul al-Fiqh and explain the reasoning behind the matn author's choice to present the idafi definition first.

Core Idea
Usul al-Fiqh has two definitions: idafi (compound) and laqabi (title); the order of presentation is a methodological choice between originality and efficiency.

In this passage, the commentator elaborates on the two ways the term 'Usul al-Fiqh' can be defined. The idafi definition treats the phrase as a compound of 'usul' and 'fiqh', each defined separately. The laqabi definition treats the entire phrase as a single proper noun for the science. The discussion centers on which definition should be presented first, with the matn author choosing the idafi for reasons related to origin (manqul 'anhu) and to avoid repetition.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two definitions
Recognise that Usul al-Fiqh has both an idafi (compound construct) and a laqabi (title) meaning. The idafi meaning is the original, while the laqabi is a transferred proper name.
This distinction is fundamental to understanding definitions in usul al-fiqh.
2
Analyze the idafi definition
In the idafi sense, 'usul' is the plural of 'asl' (foundation) and 'fiqh' is Islamic jurisprudence. The definition requires defining each part separately.
The idafi definition is 'manqul 'anhu' – the original meaning.
3
Analyze the laqabi definition
In the laqabi sense, 'Usul al-Fiqh' is a proper noun for the science of the principles of jurisprudence. It is defined as a whole, e.g., 'knowledge of the principles by which one reaches fiqh'.
The laqabi definition is 'manqul ilayh' – the transferred meaning.
4
Examine the order debate
Some scholars prefer laqabi first because in proper nouns the technical meaning is primary and because it is simpler. The matn author prefers idafi first because it is the original and to avoid defining 'fiqh' twice.
The two reasons: manqul 'anhu precedes manqul ilayh; pedagogical efficiency.
5
Apply the distinction
Be able to explain why the author chose idafi first and how this affects the structure of definitions in usul al-fiqh texts.
This prepares you to evaluate other definitions in the discipline.

مرکب اضافي له بكل اعتبار تعريف . قدم بعضهم التعريف اللقبى نظرا إلى المعنى العلمي هو المقصود في الأعلام ، وأنه من الإضافي بمنزلة البسيط من المركب . والمصنف قدم الإضافي نظرا إلى المنقول عنه مقدم ، وإلى أن الفقه ماخوذ في تعريف اللقبى فإن قدم تفسيره أمكن ذكره في اللقبي ، كما قال المصنف هو العلم بالقواعد التي يتوصل بها إلى الفقه . والاحتياج الى إيراد تفسير تارة في اللقبى وتارة في الإضافي كما في أصول ابن الحاجب " .

تشریح
شارح رحمہ اللہ متن کی تحقیق بیان کرنا چاہتے ہیں کہ اصول الفقہ کے لفظ کی ماتن نے دو ترکیبیں بیان کی ہیں (۱) هذا أصول الفقہ اس ترکیب پر مبتدا محذوف کی خبر بنے گا (۲) اصول الفقه ما هی ؟ اس وقت ترکیب پر أصول الفقه مبتدا ہو گا اور خبر محذوف ہوگی ۔ علامہ شارج ہر ایک ترکیب کی توجیہ و تشریح کرنا چاہتے ہیں کہ جب ماقبل میں کہا گیا کہ کسی علم کو جاننے کے لیے جهة واحدسه یعنی تعریف کو جاننا ضروری ہے تو طالب علم کو تعریف معلوم کرنے کا شوق پیدا ہوا قبل اس کے کہ تعریف کا سوال کر بیٹھے مصنف ماتن نے طالب کو سوال کرنے کی تکلیف نہیں دی از خود جوا با فرمایا "هذا أصول الفقه ... إلخ یہ پہلی ترکیب کی توجیہ ہے۔
دوسری ترکیب کی توجیہ یوں ہے کہ ماتن نے اپنی طرف سے أصـول الـفـقـه مـا هـي ؟ کاسوال بناتے ہوئے تعریف شروع کر دی۔ پھر فرماتے ہیں کہ لفظ أصول الفقه در حقیقت مرکب اضافی ہے۔ بعد میں اس کو منقول کر کے ایک علم دینی کا لقب قرار دیا گیا جیسا کہ لفظ عبد الله اصل کے اعتبار سے مرکب اضافی ہے جس کا معنی ہے بندہ خدا ، لیکن بعد میں اس کو نقل کر کے ایک شخص کا لقب بنادیا گیا۔ چونکہ اصول فقہ اصل کے اعتبار سے مرکب اضافی ہے اور بعد میں ایک علم دینی کا لقب ہو گیا ہے
لہذ اس کی ہر اعتبار سے تعریف کی گئی ہے : پہلی تعریف اضافی ہے جس میں مضاف و مضاف الیہ ہر ایک کی جدا جدا تعریف کی جائے ۔ دوسری تعریف لقمی ہے جس میں مجموعہ من حیث المجموع جس علم کا لقب ہے اسکی تعریف کی جائے ۔ پھر بعض حضرات تعریف لقمی کو مقدم کرتے ہیں اس کی دو وجوہیں ہیں پہلی وجہ یہ ہے کہ اعلام میں معنی لقمی معتبر ہوتا ہے جس طرح عبد اللہ اب اس کا معنی لقمی مراد ہے نہ کہ معنی اضافی (بندہ خدا ) والا مراد ہے لہذا معنی مقصودی کو مقدم ہونا چاہیے دوسری یہ کہ معنی لقی مفرد (بسیط ) ہے اور معنی اضافی مرکب ہے اور مفرد کومرکب پر تقدم حاصل ہوتا ہے۔
مصنف ماتن نے تعریف اضافی کو مقدم کیا ہے اس کی بھی دور نہیں ہیں ایک یہ کہ تعریف اضافی منقول عنہ ہے اور تعریف لقمی منقول الیہ ہے اور قانون ہے کہ منقول عنہ مقدم ہوتا ہے۔ دوسری یہ کہ تکرار سے بچنے کے لیے کیونکہ تعریف لقمی ہے " هو العلم بالقواعد التي يتوصل بها إلى الفقه " اب اگر تعریف لقمی کو مقدم کیا جاتا تو اس کو سمجھانے کے لیے لفظ فقہ کا ایک بار یہاں معنی بیان کرنا پڑتا اور دوبارہ پھر تعریف اضافی بیان کرتے وقت، کیونکہ تعریف اضافی میں ہر ہر جزء کی تعریف کرنا ہوتی ہے، اس سے خواہ خواہ تکرار لازم آتا جیسا کہ علامہ ابن حاجب کی "کتاب الأصول “ میں کیا گی ہے، اس لیے مائن نے تعریف اضافی کو جب مقدم کیا اور اس میں فقہ کی تعریف بیان کر دی تو دوبارہ تعریف تعمی میں اس کے تکرار کی ضرورت باقی نہ رہی۔
قال الشارح : " ولما كان أصول الفقه عند قصد المعنى الإضافي جمعا ، وعند قصد المعنى اللقبى مفردا كعبد الله قال : فنعرفها أولا باعتبار الإضافة بتأنيث الضمير ، وقال : فالآن نعرفه باعتبار أنه لقب لعلم مخصوص بتذكيره و اللقب “علم شعر بمدح أو ذم . " وأصول الفقه “علم لهذا الفن مشعر بكونه مبنى الفقه الذي به نظام المعاش و
نجاة المعاد وذلك مدح “ .
تشریح
مذکورہ عبارت میں ایک سوال کا جواب ہے۔ سوال یہ ہے کہ مائن نے جب اصول فقہ کی تعریف
Dars-e-Talweeh. The compound construct (murakkab idafi) has a definition in every respect. Some scholars presented the laqabi definition considering that the technical meaning is the intended one in proper nouns, and that it (the laqabi) is to the idafi like the simple to the compound. The author presented the idafi considering that the original (manqul 'anhu) comes first, and that 'fiqh' is included in the laqabi definition; if its explanation is presented, it can be mentioned in the laqabi, as the author said: 'It is the knowledge of the principles by which one reaches fiqh.' And the need to present the explanation sometimes in the laqabi and sometimes in the idafi, as in Ibn al-Hajib's Usul. Lexical investigation: 'tashawwaqat' is a feminine singular past form of 'tashawwuq' meaning 'to desire'; 'ighna' means 'to make independent'; 'basit' means 'single, having no parts'. Commentary: The commentator wants to explain the matn's investigation that the author gave two constructions for the word Usul al-Fiqh: (1) 'This is Usul al-Fiqh' where it becomes the predicate of a deleted subject; (2) 'What is Usul al-Fiqh?' where Usul al-Fiqh becomes the subject and the predicate is deleted. The commentator explains each construction: when previously it was said that to know any science one needs to know its definition, the student becomes desirous of knowing the definition; before the student asks, the matn author relieves him by answering 'This is Usul al-Fiqh...' etc. This is the explanation of the first construction. The explanation of the second construction: the matn author made the question 'What is Usul al-Fiqh?' from his side and began the definition. Then he says that the word 'Usul al-Fiqh' is in reality a compound construct. Later it was transferred and made a title for a religious science, just like the word 'Abdullah' originally is a compound construct meaning 'servant of God', but later it was transferred and became a person's name. Since Usul al-Fiqh originally is a compound construct and later became a title for a religious science, therefore it is defined in both aspects: the first is the idafi definition wherein each part (mudaf and mudaf ilayh) is defined separately; the second is the laqabi definition wherein the whole as a collective is defined as the title of a science. Then some scholars present the laqabi definition first for two reasons: first, in proper nouns the laqabi meaning is considered—just as 'Abdullah' now its laqabi meaning is intended, not the idafi meaning (servant of God)—so the intended meaning should be presented first; second, the laqabi meaning is singular (simple) and the idafi meaning is compound, and the singular takes precedence over the compound. The author of the matn presented the idafi definition first for two reasons: first, the idafi definition is the original (manqul 'anhu) and the laqabi definition is the transferred (manqul ilayh), and the rule is that the original is presented first; second, to avoid repetition, because the laqabi definition is 'It is the knowledge of the principles by which one reaches fiqh'. If the laqabi definition were presented first, one would have to explain the meaning of 'fiqh' once here and again when presenting the idafi definition, because in the idafi definition each part must be defined, leading to unavoidable repetition—as done in Ibn al-Hajib's Kitab al-Usul. Therefore, when the author presented the idafi first and explained fiqh within it, there remained no need for repetition in the laqabi definition. The commentator said: 'And since Usul al-Fiqh when intending the idafi meaning is plural, and when intending the laqabi meaning is singular like Abdullah, he said: We define it (feminine) first with the feminine pronoun considering the idafi, and he said: Now we define it (masculine) considering it is a title for a specific science with the masculine pronoun. And 'laqab' is a sign by which something is praised or dispraised. 'Usul al-Fiqh' is a sign for this art, indicating that it is the foundation of fiqh by which worldly order and salvation in the afterlife are achieved, and that is praise.' Commentary: The mentioned passage answers a question. The question is that when the author gave the definition of Usul al-Fiqh...
Source pages p. 59

Commentary
This passage is an expansion of the matn's statement regarding the definition of Usul al-Fiqh. The commentator first explains that the term 'Usul al-Fiqh' can be considered in two ways: as a compound construct (idafi) and as a title (laqabi). In the idafi sense, 'usul' is plural of 'asl' meaning foundations, and 'fiqh' is Islamic jurisprudence; the definition then requires defining each part separately. In the laqabi sense, the term as a whole is a proper name for a specific science, so it is defined collectively. The passage then discusses the order: some scholars prefer the laqabi definition first because in proper nouns the technical meaning is primary, and because the laqabi meaning is simple (singular) while the idafi is compound. However, the matn author (al-Quduri? actually the author of the matn being commented on) chose to present the idafi definition first for two reasons: (1) the idafi is the original (manqul 'anhu) and the laqabi is the transferred (manqul ilayh), and the original has precedence; (2) to avoid repetition, since the laqabi definition includes the word 'fiqh', which would have to be defined again in the idafi definition, causing redundancy. The commentator also notes the grammatical nuance: when using the idafi sense, the pronoun for 'Usul al-Fiqh' is feminine (since 'usul' is plural and treated as feminine singular in some contexts), but when using the laqabi sense, the pronoun is masculine (since the science itself is masculine in Arabic). The passage ends with a quote from the sharh explaining that 'laqab' is a sign of praise or dispraise, and that 'Usul al-Fiqh' is a praise because it is the foundation of fiqh, which brings worldly order and salvation. This passage teaches us that the definition of a technical term can be approached historically (the original compound meaning) and technically (the transferred title meaning), and that the order of presentation is a methodological choice based on pedagogic and linguistic considerations.

Key Terms
أصول الفقه (usul al-fiqh): In the idafi sense: the principles (plural of 'asl') of Islamic jurisprudence (fiqh); in the laqabi sense: the specific science that studies these principles.
مرکب اضافي (murakkab idafi): A compound construct consisting of two nouns in a possessive relationship (mudaf and mudaf ilayh), like 'Abdullah' or 'Usul al-Fiqh'.
لقب (laqab): A title or proper name given to a person or science, indicating praise or dispraise; here it is the technical name for the science of usul al-fiqh.
منقول عنه / منقول اليه (manqul 'anhu / manqul ilayh): The original meaning from which transfer occurs (manqul 'anhu) and the new meaning to which transfer occurs (manqul ilayh). For 'Usul al-Fiqh', the idafi meaning is the original, and the laqabi is the transferred.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the primary reason the matn author presented the idafi definition of Usul al-Fiqh first?
A) Because the laqabi definition is always redundant.
B) Because the idafi definition is the original (manqul 'anhu) and to avoid repetition.
C) Because the laqabi definition is grammatically incorrect.
D) Because the idafi definition is simpler and easier to understand.

Key Takeaway
The idafi definition of Usul al-Fiqh is the original compound meaning; the laqabi is the transferred title meaning; the matn author presents idafi first due to origin and efficiency.

Method of Learning
intermediate
8 min
Two Definitions of Usul al-Fiqh: Idafi and Laqabi
Explaining the two definitional approaches and the matn's arrangement

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between idafi and laqabi definitions, explain why the matn author gave precedence to the idafi, and identify the grammatical shift in pronoun usage based on the conceptual treatment of 'Usul al-Fiqh'.

Core Idea
A compound term like 'Usul al-Fiqh' can be defined by its parts (idafi) or as a whole (laqabi); the order reflects methodological priorities.

When defining a compound term like 'Usul al-Fiqh', scholars employ two approaches: the idafi definition (analyzing each component separately) and the laqabi definition (treating the term as a proper name for a science). The matn author, following the Hanafi tradition, placed the idafi definition first. This lesson unpacks the reasoning behind that choice and the subtle shift in pronoun usage that accompanies each definitional perspective.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two definitions
Locate in the passage where the idafi and laqabi definitions are introduced. The idafi definition defines 'usul' and 'fiqh' separately; the laqabi defines the whole as a title for a science.
These two methods are foundational in Hanafi usul works.
2
Understand the reasons for ordering
The passage lists two reasons for preferring the idafi first: (1) the idafi is the original (manqul 'anhu) and the laqabi is derived (manqul ilayh); (2) to avoid repetition of the definition of 'fiqh' later. Also note the opposing view that some scholars prefer the laqabi first.
Consider why avoidance of repetition is a valid pedagogical concern.
3
Analyze the pronoun shift
The matn uses a feminine pronoun ('nu'arrifuha') for the idafi definition and a masculine pronoun ('nu'arrifuhu') for the laqabi. Explain why: idafi treats the term as plural (two distinct parts), laqabi treats it as a singular entity.
This grammatical detail reflects a conceptual shift.
4
Understand the definition of laqab and the requirements of idafi definition
The passage defines 'laqab' as a sign indicating praise or blame, and notes that 'Usul al-Fiqh' is a laqab because it praises the science. For the idafi definition, the commentator explains the need to define mudaf and mudaf ilayh and the importance of the 'perspective' (haythiyya) to restrict the relation.
The concept of haythiyya is crucial in relational definitions.

تشریح
مذکورہ عبارت میں ایک سوال کا جواب ہے۔ سوال یہ ہے کہ مائن نے جب اصول فقہ کی تعریف
اضافی شروع کی تو فرمایا "فنعرفها " یعنی مونٹ کی ضمیر اصول فقہ کی طرف راجع کی ہے اور آگے جا کر جب تعریف القمی شروع کی ہے تو فرمایا " الآن نعرفه " ذکر کی ضمیر لائے ہیں یہ فرق کیوں کیا ہے؟
جواب:
تعریف اضافی کے وقت اصول فقہ کا لفظ جمع کے حکم میں ہے اس لیے کہ مضاف و مضاف الیہ کی الگ الگ تعریف کی ہے اور تعریف لقمی کے وقت مفرد کی تاویل میں ہے کیونکہ اس وقت مجموع من حیث المجموع مراد ہے جو کہ حکما مفرد ہے، جیسے عبداللہ بن وہاں پریمیر مذکرکی لاتی ہے۔ لقب کا لفظ بار بار کر آیا ہے، آخر میں لقب کی تعریف کرنا چاہتے ہیں کہ لقب وہ علم ہے جو کسی بھی کی مدح یا زم پر دال ہو۔ اصل بات یہ ہے کہ اسم تین قسم کے ہوتے ہیں کنیت علم اور لقب ۔ وجہ حصر یہ ہے کہ دیکھیں گے کہ اسم لفظ اب، ابن یا ام کے ساتھ شروع کیا گیا ہے یا نہیں اگر ابتدا میں ابن ، اب یا ام کا لفظ ہے تو وہ کنیت ہے اور اگر مذکورہ الفاظ میں سے کوئی نہیں تو پھر دیکھیں گے کہ وہ اسم سمی کی مدح اور ذم پر دلالت کرہا ہے یا نہیں ؟ اگر دلالت کر رہا ہے تو لقب، وگرنہ علم ہے، تو علم اصول فقہ ایسے اہم علم فقہ کے لیے مدار اور مہنیے جس
کے ساتھ دنیا کا انتظام اور آخرت کی نجات وابستہ ہے تو یہ اس کی مدح ہے۔
قال الشارح : " أمـا تـعـريـفها باعتبار الإضافة فيحتاج إلى تعريف المضاف وهو الأصول، وتعريف المضاف إليه وهو الفقه ، لأن تعريف المركب يحتاج إلى تعريف مفرداته الغبر البينة ضرورة توقف معرفة الكل على معرفة أجزائه ، ويحتاج إلى تعريف الإضافة ايضا لأنه بمنزلة الجزء الصورى إلا أنهم لم يتعرضوا له ، للعلم بأن معنى إضافة المشتق وما في معناه : اختصاص المضاف بالمضاف إليه باعتبار مفهوم المضاف ، مثلا : دليل المسألة ما يختص بهذا ، باعتبار كونه دليلا عليها ، فأصل الفقه ما يختص به من حيث أنه مبتنى عليه و مستندا إليه . فالأصول جمع أصل وهو في اللغة ما يبتني عليه الشئ من حيث يبتنى عليه . و بهذ االقيد خرج أدلة الفقه مثلا من حيث هي تبتني على علم التوحيد فإنها بهذا لاعتبار فروع الأصول . وقيد الحيثية لا بد منه في تعريف الإضافيات إلا أنه كثيرا ما يحذف بشهرة أمره .
In Talwih: Therefore it has been defined from every perspective: The first definition is idafi (relative), in which each of the mudaf and mudaf ilayh are defined separately. The second definition is laqabi (agnominal), in which the totality as a whole is defined as the title of that science. Then some scholars prefer the laqabi definition, for two reasons: First, that in proper nouns the agnominal meaning is considered, like 'Abdullah, here its agnominal meaning is intended, not the relative meaning (servant of God); therefore the intended meaning should be given precedence. Second, that the agnominal meaning is simple (singular) and the relative meaning is compound, and the simple has precedence over the compound. The author of the matn gave precedence to the idafi definition, for two reasons as well: First, that the idafi definition is the original (manqul 'anhu) and the laqabi definition is derived (manqul ilayh), and the rule is that the original takes precedence. Second, to avoid repetition, because the laqabi definition is 'It is the science of the principles through which one arrives at fiqh.' Now if the laqabi definition were given first, to explain it, the word fiqh would have to be defined once here, and again later when explaining the idafi definition, because in the idafi definition every part must be defined, thus repetition would necessarily occur, as done by Allamah Ibn Hajib in his book 'al-Usul'. Therefore, when the author gave precedence to the idafi definition and explained the definition of fiqh in it, the need for repetition in the laqabi definition remained no more. The commentator said: 'Since 'Usul al-Fiqh' when intending the relative meaning is plural, and when intending the agnominal meaning is singular like 'Abdullah, he said: We first define it (feminine) in consideration of the relative construction, and he said: Now we define it (masculine) in consideration of it being a title for a specific science, and al-laquab is 'a sign known for praise or blame'. And 'Usul al-Fiqh' as a science of this art indicates that it is the foundation of fiqh, upon which the order of livelihood and salvation in the afterlife depend, and that is praise.' Explanation: In the aforementioned passage is an answer to a question. The question is: When the author began the idafi definition of Usul al-Fiqh, he said 'fa-nu'arrifuha' (feminine pronoun) referring to Usul al-Fiqh, and later when he began the laqabi definition he said 'al-ana nu'arrifuhu' (masculine pronoun). Why this difference? Answer: At the time of the idafi definition, the word 'Usul al-Fiqh' is in the rule of plural because the mudaf and mudaf ilayh are defined separately, and at the time of the laqabi definition it is interpreted as singular because then the totality as a whole is intended, which is in effect singular, like 'Abdullah, where a masculine pronoun is used. The word 'laqab' is repeated. At the end, he intends to define 'laqab': it is a sign that indicates praise or blame of anyone. The basic matter is that names are of three types: kunyat, 'alam, and laqab. The reason for enumeration is that we see whether the name begins with the word 'ab', 'ibn', or 'umm'; if it begins with 'ibn', 'ab', or 'umm', then it is a kunyat; if not, then we see if the name indicates praise or blame of the named; if it indicates, then it is a laqab; otherwise it is an 'alam. So the science of Usul al-Fiqh is such an important science, the foundation and basis of fiqh, with which the order of this world and salvation in the afterlife are connected, so this is its praise. The commentator said: 'As for defining it by way of idafi, it requires defining the mudaf which is al-usul, and defining the mudaf ilayh which is al-fiqh, because defining a compound requires defining its non-obvious parts, since knowledge of the whole depends on knowledge of its parts. It also requires defining the idafa (construct) because it is like a formal part, except that they did not address it, because it is known that the meaning of idafa of a derived word and what is like it is: the specification of the mudaf to the mudaf ilayh in consideration of the concept of the mudaf. For example, 'dalil al-mas'ala' (proof of the issue) is what is specific to it, in consideration of it being a proof for it. So 'asl al-fiqh' is what is specific to it in terms of being founded upon it and based upon it. So al-usul is plural of asl, which linguistically is what something is built upon, in terms of it being built upon it. By this restriction, the proofs of fiqh are excluded, for from the perspective that they are based on the science of tawhid, they are in this consideration branches of usul. The restriction of 'perspective' (haythiyya) is necessary in defining relational terms, except that it is often omitted due to its fame.'
Source pages p. 60

Commentary
This passage is from the sharh (commentary) on the matn of Usul al-Fiqh, explaining the two ways to define the discipline: the idafi definition (by analyzing the components 'usul' and 'fiqh' separately) and the laqabi definition (treating 'Usul al-Fiqh' as a proper name for a specific science). The author of the matn preferred the idafi definition first. The commentator offers two rationales: first, that the idafi definition is the original (manqul 'anhu) from which the laqabi is derived, and the original takes precedence in ordering; second, to avoid repetition of the definition of 'fiqh' if the laqabi definition were given first. Then the commentator addresses a grammatical issue: the matn uses a feminine pronoun ('nufarrifuha') for the idafi definition and a masculine pronoun ('nufarrifuhu') for the laqabi definition. The reason is that in the idafi sense, 'Usul al-Fiqh' is treated as a plural (because two distinct things are defined), whereas in the laqabi sense it is a single entity (a title), thus masculine singular. Finally, the nature of 'laqab' is explained: it is a sign indicating praise or blame. Names are divided into kunyat (with 'ab', 'ibn', 'umm'), 'alam (neutral proper name), and laqab (indicating praise or blame). Since 'Usul al-Fiqh' indicates praise (for being the foundation of worldly order and afterlife salvation), it is a laqab. The commentator then details the requirements of an idafi definition: defining the mudaf (usul) and mudaf ilayh (fiqh), and mentioning the perspective (haythiyya) to restrict the relation.

Key Terms
تعریف اضافی (ta'rif idafi): A definition that analyzes a compound term by defining each part separately, e.g., defining 'usul' and 'fiqh' individually.
تعریف لقمی (ta'rif laqabi): A definition that treats the compound term as a single proper name with praise or blame, e.g., defining 'Usul al-Fiqh' as a science without analyzing components.
لقب (laqab): A sign (name) that indicates praise or blame of the named person or thing.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why did the matn author use a feminine pronoun (nu'arrifuha) for the idafi definition of Usul al-Fiqh?
A) Because 'usul' is feminine in Arabic.
B) Because 'Usul al-Fiqh' is treated as a plural when considering its parts.
C) Because the science of Usul al-Fiqh is considered a single entity.
D) Because the author made a grammatical error.

Key Takeaway
The idafi and laqabi definitions of Usul al-Fiqh represent two distinct methodological approaches; the matn author's preference for idafi-first is justified by originality and avoidance of repetition, and the pronoun shift highlights the conceptual difference between analyzing parts and treating the term as a unified whole.

Method of Learning
intermediate
8 min
The Necessity of Defining Parts in the Idafi Definition
Explains the need to define each part of the compound term

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why a compound term in idafi definition requires defining its unclear components separately, and why the idafa itself is not defined, according to Hanafi usul methodology.

Core Idea
A compound definition demands clarifying its parts; the idafa is omitted because its meaning is intuitively understood.

When defining 'usul al-fiqh' via idafa (construct state), the scholars of usul teach us that we must first define each part that is not immediately clear. But why is the construct relationship (idafa) itself left undefined? This lesson unpacks the Hanafi approach to compound definitions and the intuitive nature of the idafa.

Guided Path
1
Distinguish the two types of definitions
In the matn, two approaches are mentioned: the idafi definition (definition by construct) and the laqabi definition (definition as a title). Recognize that in the laqabi definition, the term is treated as a singular proper noun, while in the idafi it is a compound.
2
Apply the rule for compounds
The commentator states: 'defining a compound requires defining its components that are not clear.' This is because understanding the whole depends on understanding its parts. So for 'usul al-fiqh', we need definitions for 'usul' and 'fiqh'.
The parts must be 'non-obvious' (ghayr bayyinah).
3
Explain why the idafa itself is not defined
The idafa (the construct relationship) is like a formal part, but the authors omitted it because its meaning is intuitively understood: the mudaf is specific to the mudaf ilayh with respect to its concept. This is considered well-known and thus unnecessary to define.
4
Contrast with the laqabi definition
In the laqabi definition, the term is taken as a whole, like a title (laqab). The passage then defines laqab as a name indicating praise or dispraise, and distinguishes it from kunyah and 'alam. This shows that the same term can be defined differently depending on the perspective.

Source Text

تعريف اضافي کے وقت اصول فقہ کا لفظ جمع کے حکم میں ہے اس لیے کہ مضاف و مضاف الیہ کی الگ الگ تعریف کی ہے اور تعریف لقبی کے وقت مفرد کی تاویل میں ہے کیونکہ اس وقت مجموع من حیث المجموع مراد ہے جو کہ حکما مفرد ہے، جیسے عبداللہ بن وہاں پریمیر مذکرکی لاتی ہے۔ لقب کا لفظ بار بار کر آیا ہے، آخر میں لقب کی تعریف کرنا چاہتے ہیں کہ لقب وہ علم ہے جو کسی بھی کی مدح یا زم پر دال ہو۔ اصل بات یہ ہے کہ اسم تین قسم کے ہوتے ہیں کنیت علم اور لقب ۔ وجہ حصر یہ ہے کہ دیکھیں گے کہ اسم لفظ اب، ابن یا ام کے ساتھ شروع کیا گیا ہے یا نہیں اگر ابتدا میں ابن ، اب یا ام کا لفظ ہے تو وہ کنیت ہے اور اگر مذکورہ الفاظ میں سے کوئی نہیں تو پھر دیکھیں گے کہ وہ اسم سمی کی مدح اور ذم پر دلالت کرہا ہے یا نہیں ؟ اگر دلالت کر رہا ہے تو لقب، وگرنہ علم ہے، تو علم اصول فقہ ایسے اہم علم فقہ کے لیے مدار اور مہنیے جس کے ساتھ دنیا کا انتظام اور آخرت کی نجات وابستہ ہے تو یہ اس کی مدح ہے۔
قال الشارح : " أمـا تـعـريـفها باعتبار الإضافة فيحتاج إلى تعريف المضاف وهو الأصول، وتعريف المضاف إليه وهو الفقه ، لأن تعريف المركب يحتاج إلى تعريف مفرداته الغبر البينة ضرورة توقف معرفة الكل على معرفة أجزائه ، ويحتاج إلى تعريف الإضافة ايضا لأنه بمنزلة الجزء الصورى إلا أنهم لم يتعرضوا له ، للعلم بأن معنى إضافة المشتق وما في معناه : اختصاص المضاف بالمضاف إليه باعتبار مفهوم المضاف ، مثلا : دليل المسألة ما يختص بهذا ، باعتبار كونه دليلا عليها ، فأصل الفقه ما يختص به من حيث أنه مبتنى عليه و مستندا إليه . فالأصول جمع أصل وهو في اللغة ما يبتني عليه الشئ من حيث يبتنى عليه . و بهذ االقيد خرج أدلة الفقه مثلا من حيث هي تبتني على علم التوحيد فإنها بهذا لاعتبار فروع الأصول . وقيد الحيثية لا بد منه في تعريف الإضافيات إلا أنه كثيرا ما يحذف بشهرة أمره .
تشريح
ماتن نے کہا کہ تعریف اضافی کرتے وقت ہم مضاف و مضاف الیہ ہر ایک کی جدا جدا تعریف کریں گے یہاں سے علامہ شارح اس کی وجہ بیان کر رہے ہیں کہ اضافت میں ترکیب ہوتی ہے لہذا ہر مرکب کو معلوم کرنے کے لیے ضروری ہے کہ اس کے ہر غیر واضح اور مبہم جز ء کو واضح کیا جاوے ہمثلا: مضاف کو بیان کیا جائے پھر مضاف الیہ کو ۔ اس لیے کہ کل کا سمجھنا اجزاء کے سمجھنے پر موقوف ہوتا ہے یہاں پر ماتن نے جس طرح مضاف و مضاف الیہ کی تعریف بیان کی ہے اس کو چاہیے تھا کہ اضافت کی بھی تعریف کرتے ۔ اس لیے کہ اضافت مرکب اضافی کے لیے بمنزلہ جزء صوری کے ہے مگر ماتن نے بیان نہیں کی کیونکہ ہر ایک کو معلوم ہے کہ مشتق یا جو مشتق کے معنی میں ہو جب اس کو مضاف کیا جاوے تو اس کا معنی بداہتہ یہی ہے کہ مضاف کا جو بھی معنی ہے اس اعتبار سے وہ مضاف الیہ کے ساتھ خاص ہے، مثلا: أصول الفقه یعنی وہ ادلہ جو فقہ کے ساتھ خاص ہیں اور فقہ ان پر مبنی ہے اور ان کی طرف مستند ہے کیونکہ اصول اصل کی جمع ہے جس کا معنی ہے وہ بھی جس پر دوسری بھی کی بناء ہو جائیں حیثیت کہ یہ ھی اس کی طرف محتاج ہو آخر میں ”و بهذا القيد ...الخ " سے ایک اعتراض دفع کرنا چاہتے ہیں اعتراض یہ ہے آپ نے ادلہ فقہ ( کتاب، سنت، اجماع، قیاس) کو فقہ کا مینی قرار دیا ہے اور اس وجہ سے آپ ان کو اصول کہتے ہیں حالانکہ یہی اولہ علم التوحید پر مبنی ہوتے ہیں، کیونکہ جب تک خداوند تعالی کے وجود اور صفات کو ثابت نہ کیا جائے ، جن کا محل بیان علم التوحید ہے اسوقت تک ادلہ اربعہ ( قرآن، سنت، اجماع، قیاس ) کا وجود ثابت نہیں ہو سکتا۔ الحاصل ادلہ فقہ منی نہ بنے بلکہ خود محتاج ہو کر مبنی علی الغیر ہوئے لہذا ان کو اصول کہنا درست نہیں جواب کا حاصل یہ ہے کہ ان کو اصول کہنا بنسبت فقہ کے ہے اگر چہ یہ خود علم التوحید پر مبنی ہو کر فروع میں بھی شمار ہوتے ہیں مگر وہ دوسری حیثیت کے اعتبار سے ہے ۔ اس لیے کہا گیا کہ اصل کی تعریف میں حیثیت کی قید بڑھانی چاہیے تعریف یوں کرنی چاہیے "ما بستنی عليه غيره من حيث يبتنی علیه غیرہ " کیونکہ اس قسم کے نسبی امور میں حیثیت کی قید بڑھانا ضروری ہوتا ہے مگر بسا اوقات شہرت کی بناء پر چھوڑ دیتے ہیں۔
قال الشارح : " ثم نقل الأصل في العرف إلى معان أخر ، مثل الراجح ، والقاعدة
At the time of the additional definition, the word 'usul al-fiqh' is in the ruling of a plural because it defines the mudaf and mudaf ilayh separately, and at the time of the laqabi definition, it is in the interpretation of a singular because then the whole from the perspective of the whole is intended, which is singular in terms of ruling, just like 'Abdullah ibn where the masculine pronoun is used. The word 'laqab' has been repeated many times; at the end, they intend to define laqab: that laqab is a name that indicates praise or dispraise of someone. The basic point is that names are of three types: kunyah, 'alam, and laqab. The reason for the restriction is that we consider whether the name begins with the word 'ab', 'ibn', or 'umm'. If it begins with 'ibn', 'ab', or 'umm', it is a kunyah. If none of these words are present, then we consider whether the name indicates praise or dispraise of the one named. If it does, it is a laqab; otherwise, it is an 'alam. Thus, the knowledge of usul al-fiqh is such an important knowledge, the pivot and foundation for fiqh, with which the management of this world and the salvation of the afterlife are connected, so this is its praise.
The commentator said: "As for its definition by way of idafa (construct state), it requires defining the mudaf (the first part) which is 'usul', and defining the mudaf ilayh (the second part) which is 'fiqh', because defining a compound requires defining its components that are not clear, due to the necessity that knowing the whole depends on knowing its parts. It also requires defining the idafa itself, because it is like a formal part, except that they did not address it, because it is known that the meaning of idafa of a derivative and what is in its meaning is the special relationship of the mudaf to the mudaf ilayh with respect to the concept of the mudaf. For example, 'the proof of the issue' is what is specific to it, in terms of being a proof for it. So 'usul al-fiqh' is what is specific to it in that it is based upon it and refers to it. So 'usul' is the plural of 'asl', which in language is that upon which something is built, in terms of being built upon it. With this qualification, the proofs of fiqh, for example, are excluded from being 'usul' from the perspective that they are built upon the science of tawhid, for in that consideration they are branches of usul. The qualification of perspective is necessary in the definition of relative terms, except that it is often omitted due to its being well-known."
Clarification: The matn said that when making an additional definition, we will define the mudaf and mudaf ilayh separately. From here, the commentator explains the reason: because in idafa there is a compound, so to know every compound, it is necessary to clarify each unclear and ambiguous part, for example, to explain the mudaf, then the mudaf ilayh. This is because understanding the whole depends on understanding the parts. Here, the matn defined the mudaf and mudaf ilayh; it should have also defined the idafa itself, because the idafa is like a formal part of the compound. However, the matn did not mention it because everyone knows that when a derivative or what is in the meaning of a derivative is used in idafa, its intuitive meaning is that the mudaf, whatever its meaning, is specific to the mudaf ilayh with respect to that meaning. For example, 'usul al-fiqh' means the proofs that are specific to fiqh, and fiqh is based on them and refers to them. Because 'usul' is the plural of 'asl', which means that upon which another thing is built, in the sense that it depends on it. At the end, with "and with this qualification...", they intend to repel an objection. The objection is: You have considered the proofs of fiqh (Book, Sunnah, consensus, analogy) as the foundation of fiqh and therefore call them 'usul', whereas these themselves are built upon the science of tawhid, because until the existence and attributes of Allah are established, which is the subject of the science of tawhid, the four proofs cannot exist. In conclusion, the proofs of fiqh are not foundations; rather, they themselves are dependent and built upon something else, so calling them 'usul' is not correct. The answer is that they are called 'usul' relative to fiqh, even though they themselves are built upon the science of tawhid and are considered branches from that perspective. Therefore, it is said that in the definition of 'asl', the qualification of perspective should be added: the definition should be 'that upon which something else is built, in terms of being built upon it'. In such relative matters, the qualification of perspective is necessary, but sometimes it is omitted due to its being well-known.
The commentator said: "Then the term 'asl' in common usage was transferred to other meanings, such as the preponderant (rajih) and the base (qa'ida)."
Source pages p. 61

Commentary
This passage is a commentary on the definition of 'usul al-fiqh' via idafa (construct state). It begins by distinguishing between two types of definitions: the idafi definition (definition by way of construct) and the laqabi definition (definition as a title). In the idafi definition, the term 'usul al-fiqh' is treated as a compound, so each part must be defined separately: 'usul' (principles) and 'fiqh' (jurisprudence). In the laqabi definition, the term is treated as a single proper noun (a laqab or title) that indicates praise for the science, since usul al-fiqh is the foundation for fiqh, which is essential for worldly and religious success. The text then discusses the division of names into kunyah (patronymic), 'alam (name), and laqab (title). The commentator explains that the matn (al-Tawdih) correctly defined the parts but omitted defining the idafa itself; however, that is because the meaning of idafa in such constructs is intuitively understood: the mudaf is specifically related to the mudaf ilayh. For example, 'usul al-fiqh' means the proofs that are specifically related to fiqh, in that fiqh is built upon them. The commentator then addresses an objection: how can the proofs of fiqh (Quran, Sunnah, consensus, analogy) be called 'usul' (principles) when they themselves are built upon the science of tawhid (theology)? The Hanafi answer is that they are principles relative to fiqh, even if they are branches from the perspective of tawhid. This is why the definition of 'asl' must include the qualification 'from the perspective of being built upon' (min haythu yabtani 'alayhi). Finally, the passage notes that the term 'asl' in common usage has been extended to other meanings like 'rajih' (preponderant) and 'qa'ida' (base rule).

Key Terms
إضافة (idafa): The grammatical construct state where a noun is related to another noun, implying specification.
أصل (asl): That upon which something else is built, in terms of being built upon it.
لقب (laqab): A name that indicates praise or dispraise of the named person.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi commentator, why is the idafa (construct) not separately defined in the idafi definition of 'usul al-fiqh'?
A) Because the idafa is not a part of the compound.
B) Because the meaning of idafa is intuitively understood: the mudaf is specific to the mudaf ilayh in terms of the concept.
C) Because the matn forgot to define it.
D) Because the idafa is defined elsewhere in the same work.

Key Takeaway
In the idafi definition of a compound term, define each unclear part separately; the idafa is omitted because its relational meaning is self-evident.

Defining 'Asl' and Repelling the Objection: The Perspective Qualification
Defines 'asl' with perspective qualification and repels an objection

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the precise Hanafi definition of 'asl' with the perspective qualification and analyze the objection that the proofs of fiqh are themselves built on tawhid, and how the Hanafi answer uses the qayd al-haythiyyah.

Core Idea
'Asl' is that upon which something is built from the very perspective of being built upon—this qualification excludes relative foundations like tawhid.

One might object that the proofs of fiqh (usul) are themselves built upon the science of tawhid, so how can they be called 'asl'? The Hanafi response lies in a subtle but crucial qualification: the definition of 'asl' includes the phrase 'from the perspective of being built upon'. This lesson unpacks that definition and shows how it resolves the apparent contradiction.

Guided Path
1
Recall the definition of 'asl'
The commentator defines 'asl' as: 'that upon which something is built, in terms of being built upon it' (ma yabtani 'alayhi al-shay' min haythu yabtani 'alayhi). Note the crucial qualifier 'min haythu yabtani 'alayhi' (from the perspective of being built upon).
2
State the objection
The objection: The proofs of fiqh (Quran, Sunnah, consensus, analogy) are themselves built upon the science of tawhid (theology), because tawhid establishes the existence and attributes of God, without which the proofs cannot be valid. So they are not truly 'asl' but 'far' (branches) from that perspective.
3
Understand the Hanafi answer
The answer is that these proofs are 'asl' relative to fiqh, not relative to tawhid. The definition of 'asl' includes the perspective qualification: something is 'asl' only in relation to that which is built upon it. The proofs are 'asl' for fiqh, even though they are 'far' for tawhid.
This is why the qualification 'min haythu yabtani 'alayhi' is necessary: it reminds us that the asl-far relationship is relative, not absolute.
4
Apply the qualification to other relative terms
The commentator notes that this qualification is necessary for all relative (idafi) definitions. For example, 'al-fiqh' itself is defined relative to its sources. Understanding this prevents confusion when the same thing is both an 'asl' in one context and a 'far' in another.

قال الشارح : " ثم نقل الأصل في العرف إلى معان أخر ، مثل الراجح ، والقاعدة
At the time of the additional definition, the word 'usul al-fiqh' is in the ruling of a plural because it defines the mudaf and mudaf ilayh separately, and at the time of the laqabi definition, it is in the interpretation of a singular because then the whole from the perspective of the whole is intended, which is singular in terms of ruling, just like 'Abdullah ibn where the masculine pronoun is used. The word 'laqab' has been repeated many times; at the end, they intend to define laqab: that laqab is a name that indicates praise or dispraise of someone. The basic point is that names are of three types: kunyah, 'alam, and laqab. The reason for the restriction is that we consider whether the name begins with the word 'ab', 'ibn', or 'umm'. If it begins with 'ibn', 'ab', or 'umm', it is a kunyah. If none of these words are present, then we consider whether the name indicates praise or dispraise of the one named. If it does, it is a laqab; otherwise, it is an 'alam. Thus, the knowledge of usul al-fiqh is such an important knowledge, the pivot and foundation for fiqh, with which the management of this world and the salvation of the afterlife are connected, so this is its praise.
The commentator said: "As for its definition by way of idafa (construct state), it requires defining the mudaf (the first part) which is 'usul', and defining the mudaf ilayh (the second part) which is 'fiqh', because defining a compound requires defining its components that are not clear, due to the necessity that knowing the whole depends on knowing its parts. It also requires defining the idafa itself, because it is like a formal part, except that they did not address it, because it is known that the meaning of idafa of a derivative and what is in its meaning is the special relationship of the mudaf to the mudaf ilayh with respect to the concept of the mudaf. For example, 'the proof of the issue' is what is specific to it, in terms of being a proof for it. So 'usul al-fiqh' is what is specific to it in that it is based upon it and refers to it. So 'usul' is the plural of 'asl', which in language is that upon which something is built, in terms of being built upon it. With this qualification, the proofs of fiqh, for example, are excluded from being 'usul' from the perspective that they are built upon the science of tawhid, for in that consideration they are branches of usul. The qualification of perspective is necessary in the definition of relative terms, except that it is often omitted due to its being well-known."
Clarification: The matn said that when making an additional definition, we will define the mudaf and mudaf ilayh separately. From here, the commentator explains the reason: because in idafa there is a compound, so to know every compound, it is necessary to clarify each unclear and ambiguous part, for example, to explain the mudaf, then the mudaf ilayh. This is because understanding the whole depends on understanding the parts. Here, the matn defined the mudaf and mudaf ilayh; it should have also defined the idafa itself, because the idafa is like a formal part of the compound. However, the matn did not mention it because everyone knows that when a derivative or what is in the meaning of a derivative is used in idafa, its intuitive meaning is that the mudaf, whatever its meaning, is specific to the mudaf ilayh with respect to that meaning. For example, 'usul al-fiqh' means the proofs that are specific to fiqh, and fiqh is based on them and refers to them. Because 'usul' is the plural of 'asl', which means that upon which another thing is built, in the sense that it depends on it. At the end, with "and with this qualification...", they intend to repel an objection. The objection is: You have considered the proofs of fiqh (Book, Sunnah, consensus, analogy) as the foundation of fiqh and therefore call them 'usul', whereas these themselves are built upon the science of tawhid, because until the existence and attributes of Allah are established, which is the subject of the science of tawhid, the four proofs cannot exist. In conclusion, the proofs of fiqh are not foundations; rather, they themselves are dependent and built upon something else, so calling them 'usul' is not correct. The answer is that they are called 'usul' relative to fiqh, even though they themselves are built upon the science of tawhid and are considered branches from that perspective. Therefore, it is said that in the definition of 'asl', the qualification of perspective should be added: the definition should be 'that upon which something else is built, in terms of being built upon it'. In such relative matters, the qualification of perspective is necessary, but sometimes it is omitted due to its being well-known.
The commentator said: "Then the term 'asl' in common usage was transferred to other meanings, such as the preponderant (rajih) and the base (qa'ida)."

Commentary

It begins by distinguishing between two types of definitions: the idafi definition (definition by way of construct) and the laqabi definition (definition as a title). Key Terms
أصل (asl): That upon which something is built, in terms of being built upon it.
حيثية (haythiyya): Perspective or consideration; a qualification that specifies the aspect from which a relationship is viewed.
فرع (far'): That which is built upon something else; the derivative or secondary.
